BUG: Variable not defined when awaited and rendered inside a snippet
### Describe the bug

I’m using the experimental `async` flag.

```
Uncaught (in promise) ReferenceError: value is not defined
```

    13	/**
    14	 * A utility for extracting complex expressions (such as call expressions)
    15	 * from templates and replacing them with `$0`, `$1` etc
    16	 */
    17	export class Memoizer {
    18	        /** @type {Array<{ id: Identifier, expression: Expression }>} */
    19	        #sync = [];
    20	
    21	        /** @type {Array<{ id: Identifier, expression: Expression }>} */
    22	        #async = [];
    23	
    24	        /**
    25	         * @param {Expression} expression
    26	         * @param {boolean} has_await
    27	         */
    28	        add(expression, has_await) {
    29	                const id = b.id('#'); // filled in later
    30	
    31	                (has_await ? this.#async : this.#sync).push({ id, expression });
    32	
    33	                return id;
    34	        }
    35	
    36	        apply() {
    37	                return [...this.#sync, ...this.#async].map((memo, i) => {
    38	                        memo.id.name = `$${i}`;
    39	                        return memo.id;
    40	                });
    41	        }
    42	
    43	        deriveds(runes = true) {
    44	                return this.#sync.map((memo) =>
    45	                        b.let(memo.id, b.call(runes ? '$.derived' : '$.derived_safe_equal', b.thunk(memo.expression)))
    46	                );
    47	        }
    48	
    49	        async_ids() {
    50	                return this.#async.map((memo) => memo.id);
    51	        }
    52	
    53	        async_values() {
    54	                if (this.#async.length === 0) return;
    55	                return b.array(this.#async.map((memo) => b.thunk(memo.expression, true)));
    56	        }
    57	
    58	        sync_values() {
    59	                if (this.#sync.length === 0) return;
    60	                return b.array(this.#sync.map((memo) => b.thunk(memo.expression)));
    61	        }
    62	}
    63	
    64	/**
    65	 * @param {Array<AST.Text | AST.ExpressionTag>} values
    66	 * @param {ComponentContext} context
    67	 * @param {ComponentClientTransformState} state
    68	 * @param {(value: Expression, metadata: ExpressionMetadata) => Expression} memoize
    69	 * @returns {{ value: Expression, has_state: boolean }}
    70	 */
    71	export function build_template_chunk(
    72	        values,
    73	        context,
    74	        state = context.state,
    75	        memoize = (value, metadata) =>
    76	                metadata.has_call || metadata.has_await ? state.memoizer.add(value, metadata.has_await) : value
    77	) {
    78	        /** @type {Expression[]} */
    79	        const expressions = [];
    80	
    81	        let quasi = b.quasi('');
    82	        const quasis = [quasi];
    83	
    84	        let has_state = false;
    85	        let has_await = false;
    86	
    87	        for (let i = 0; i < values.length; i++) {
    88	                const node = values[i];
    89	
    90	                if (node.type === 'Text') {
    91	                        quasi.value.cooked += node.data;
    92	                } else if (node.expression.type === 'Literal') {
    93	                        if (node.expression.value != null) {
    94	                                quasi.value.cooked += node.expression.value + '';
    95	                        }
    96	                } else if (
    97	                        node.expression.type !== 'Identifier' ||
    98	                        node.expression.name !== 'undefined' ||
    99	                        state.scope.get('undefined')
   100	                ) {
   101	                        let value = memoize(
   102	                                build_expression(context, node.expression, node.metadata.expression, state),
   103	                                node.metadata.expression
   104	                        );
   105	
   106	                        const evaluated = state.scope.evaluate(value);
   107	
   108	                        has_await ||= node.metadata.expression.has_await;
   109	                        has_state ||= has_await || (node.metadata.expression.has_state && !evaluated.is_known);
   110	
   111	                        if (values.length === 1) {
   112	                                // If we have a single expression, then pass that in directly to possibly avoid doing
   113	                                // extra work in the template_effect (instead we do the work in set_text).
   114	                                if (evaluated.is_known) {
   115	                                        value = b.literal((evaluated.value ?? '') + '');
   116	                                }
   117	
   118	                                return { value, has_state };
   119	                        }
   120	
   121	                        if (
   122	                                value.type === 'LogicalExpression' &&
   123	                                value.right.type === 'Literal' &&
   124	                                (value.operator === '??' || value.operator === '||')
   125	                        ) {
   126	                                // `foo ?? null` -=> `foo ?? ''`
   127	                                // otherwise leave the expression untouched
   128	                                if (value.right.value === null) {
   129	                                        value = { ...value, right: b.literal('') };
   130	                                }
   131	                        }
   132	
   133	                        if (evaluated.is_known) {
   134	                                quasi.value.cooked += (evaluated.value ?? '') + '';
   135	                        } else {
   136	                                if (!evaluated.is_defined) {
   137	                                        // add `?? ''` where necessary
   138	                                        value = b.logical('??', value, b.literal(''));
   139	                                }
   140	
   141	                                expressions.push(value);
   142	
   143	                                quasi = b.quasi('', i + 1 === values.length);
   144	                                quasis.push(quasi);
   145	                        }
   146	                }
   147	        }
   148	
   149	        for (const quasi of quasis) {
   150	                quasi.value.raw = sanitize_template_string(/** @type {string} */ (quasi.value.cooked));
   151	        }
   152	
   153	        const value =
   154	                expressions.length > 0
   155	                        ? b.template(quasis, expressions)
   156	                        : b.literal(/** @type {string} */ (quasi.value.cooked));
   157	
   158	        return { value, has_state };
   159	}

   161	/**
   162	 * @param {ComponentClientTransformState} state
   163	 */
   164	export function build_render_statement(state) {
   165	        const { memoizer } = state;
   166	
   167	        const ids = memoizer.apply();
   168	
   169	        return b.stmt(
   170	                b.call(
   171	                        '$.template_effect',
   172	                        b.arrow(
   173	                                ids,
   174	                                state.update.length === 1 && state.update[0].type === 'ExpressionStatement'
   175	                                        ? state.update[0].expression
   176	                                        : b.block(state.update)
   177	                        ),
   178	                        memoizer.sync_values(),
   179	                        memoizer.async_values()
   180	                )
   181	        );
   182	}

   184	/**
   185	 * For unfortunate legacy reasons, directive names can look like this `use:a.b-c`
   186	 * This turns that string into a member expression
   187	 * @param {string} name
   188	 */
   189	export function parse_directive_name(name) {
   190	        // this allow for accessing members of an object
   191	        const parts = name.split('.');
   192	        let part = /** @type {string} */ (parts.shift());
   193	
   194	        /** @type {Identifier | MemberExpression} */
   195	        let expression = b.id(part);
   196	
   197	        while ((part = /** @type {string} */ (parts.shift()))) {
   198	                const computed = !regex_is_valid_identifier.test(part);
   199	                expression = b.member(expression, computed ? b.literal(part) : b.id(part), computed);
   200	        }
   201	
   202	        return expression;
   203	}
   204	
   205	/**
   206	 * Serializes `bind:this` for components and elements.
   207	 * @param {Identifier | MemberExpression | SequenceExpression} expression
   208	 * @param {Expression} value
   209	 * @param {import('zimmerframe').Context<AST.SvelteNode, ComponentClientTransformState>} context
   210	 */
   211	export function build_bind_this(expression, value, { state, visit }) {
   212	        if (expression.type === 'SequenceExpression') {
   213	                const [get, set] = /** @type {SequenceExpression} */ (visit(expression)).expressions;
   214	                return b.call('$.bind_this', value, set, get);
   215	        }
   216	
   217	        /** @type {Identifier[]} */
   218	        const ids = [];
   219	
   220	        /** @type {Expression[]} */
   221	        const values = [];
   222	
   223	        /** @type {string[]} */
   224	        const seen = [];
   225	
   226	        const transform = { ...state.transform };
   227	
   228	        // Pass in each context variables to the get/set functions, so that we can null out old values on teardown.
   229	        // Note that we only do this for each context variables, the consequence is that the value might be stale in
   230	        // some scenarios where the value is a member expression with changing computed parts or using a combination of multiple
   231	        // variables, but that was the same case in Svelte 4, too. Once legacy mode is gone completely, we can revisit this.
   232	        walk(expression, null, {
   233	                Identifier(node, { path }) {
   234	                        if (seen.includes(node.name)) return;
   235	                        seen.push(node.name);
   236	
   237	                        const parent = /** @type {Expression} */ (path.at(-1));
   238	                        if (!is_reference(node, parent)) return;
   239	
   240	                        const binding = state.scope.get(node.name);
   241	                        if (!binding) return;
   242	
   243	                        for (const [owner, scope] of state.scopes) {
   244	                                if (owner.type === 'EachBlock' && scope === binding.scope) {
   245	                                        ids.push(node);
   246	                                        values.push(/** @type {Expression} */ (visit(node)));
   247	
   248	                                        if (transform[node.name]) {
   249	                                                transform[node.name] = {
   250	                                                        ...transform[node.name],
   251	                                                        read: (node) => node
   252	                                                };
   253	                                        }
   254	
   255	                                        break;
   256	                                }
   257	                        }
   258	                }
   259	        });
   260	
   261	        const child_state = { ...state, transform };
   262	
   263	        const get = /** @type {Expression} */ (visit(expression, child_state));
   264	        const set = /** @type {Expression} */ (
   265	                visit(b.assignment('=', expression, b.id('$$value')), child_state)
   266	        );
   267	
   268	        // If we're mutating a property, then it might already be non-existent.
   269	        // If we make all the object nodes optional, then it avoids any runtime exceptions.
   270	        /** @type {Expression | Super} */
   271	        let node = get;
   272	
   273	        while (node.type === 'MemberExpression') {
   274	                node.optional = true;
   275	                node = node.object;
   276	        }
   277	
   278	        return b.call(
   279	                '$.bind_this',
   280	                value,
   281	                b.arrow([b.id('$$value'), ...ids], set),
   282	                b.arrow([...ids], get),
   283	                values.length > 0 && b.thunk(b.array(values))
   284	        );
   285	}
   286	
   287	/**
   288	 * @param {ComponentClientTransformState} state
   289	 * @param {AST.BindDirective} binding
   290	 * @param {MemberExpression} expression
   291	 */
   292	export function validate_binding(state, binding, expression) {
   293	        if (binding.expression.type === 'SequenceExpression') {
   294	                return;
   295	        }
   296	        // If we are referencing a $store.foo then we don't need to add validation
   297	        const left = object(binding.expression);
   298	        const left_binding = left && state.scope.get(left.name);
   299	        if (left_binding?.kind === 'store_sub') return;
   300	
   301	        const loc = locator(binding.start);
   302	
   303	        const obj = /** @type {Expression} */ (expression.object);
   304	
   305	        state.init.push(
   306	                b.stmt(
   307	                        b.call(
   308	                                '$.validate_binding',
   309	                                b.literal(state.analysis.source.slice(binding.start, binding.end)),
   310	                                b.thunk(
   311	                                        state.store_to_invalidate ? b.sequence([b.call('$.mark_store_binding'), obj]) : obj
   312	                                ),
   313	                                b.thunk(
   314	                                        /** @type {Expression} */ (
   315	                                                expression.computed
   316	                                                        ? expression.property
   317	                                                        : b.literal(/** @type {Identifier} */ (expression.property).name)
   318	                                        )
   319	                                ),
   320	                                loc && b.literal(loc.line),
   321	                                loc && b.literal(loc.column)
   322	                        )
   323	                )
   324	        );
   325	}

   327	/**
   328	 * In dev mode validate mutations to props
   329	 * @param {AssignmentExpression | UpdateExpression} node
   330	 * @param {Context} context
   331	 * @param {Expression} expression
   332	 */
   333	export function validate_mutation(node, context, expression) {
   334	        let left = /** @type {Expression | Super} */ (
   335	                node.type === 'AssignmentExpression' ? node.left : node.argument
   336	        );
   337	
   338	        if (!dev || left.type !== 'MemberExpression' || is_ignored(node, 'ownership_invalid_mutation')) {
   339	                return expression;
   340	        }
   341	
   342	        const name = object(left);
   343	        if (!name) return expression;
   344	
   345	        const binding = context.state.scope.get(name.name);
   346	        if (binding?.kind !== 'prop' && binding?.kind !== 'bindable_prop') return expression;
   347	
   348	        const state = /** @type {ComponentClientTransformState} */ (context.state);
   349	        state.analysis.needs_mutation_validation = true;
   350	
   351	        /** @type {Array<Identifier | Literal | Expression>} */
   352	        const path = [];
   353	
   354	        while (left.type === 'MemberExpression') {
   355	                if (left.property.type === 'Literal') {
   356	                        path.unshift(left.property);
   357	                } else if (left.property.type === 'Identifier') {
   358	                        const transform = Object.hasOwn(context.state.transform, left.property.name)
   359	                                ? context.state.transform[left.property.name]
   360	                                : null;
   361	                        if (left.computed) {
   362	                                path.unshift(transform?.read ? transform.read(left.property) : left.property);
   363	                        } else {
   364	                                path.unshift(b.literal(left.property.name));
   365	                        }
   366	                } else {
   367	                        return expression;
   368	                }
   369	
   370	                left = left.object;
   371	        }
   372	
   373	        path.unshift(b.literal(name.name));
   374	
   375	        const loc = locator(/** @type {number} */ (left.start));
   376	
   377	        return b.call(
   378	                '$$ownership_validator.mutation',
   379	                b.literal(binding.prop_alias),
   380	                b.array(path),
   381	                expression,
   382	                loc && b.literal(loc.line),
   383	                loc && b.literal(loc.column)
   384	        );
   385	}
   386	
   387	/**
   388	 *
   389	 * @param {ComponentContext} context
   390	 * @param {Expression} expression
   391	 * @param {ExpressionMetadata} metadata
   392	 */
   393	export function build_expression(context, expression, metadata, state = context.state) {
   394	        const value = /** @type {Expression} */ (context.visit(expression, state));
   395	
   396	        // Components not explicitly in legacy mode might be expected to be in runes mode (especially since we didn't
   397	        // adjust this behavior until recently, which broke people's existing components), so we also bail in this case.
   398	        // Kind of an in-between-mode.
   399	        if (context.state.analysis.runes || context.state.analysis.maybe_runes) {
   400	                return value;
   401	        }
   402	
   403	        if (!metadata.has_call && !metadata.has_member_expression && !metadata.has_assignment) {
   404	                return value;
   405	        }
   406	
   407	        // Legacy reactivity is coarse-grained, looking at the statically visible dependencies. Replicate that here
   408	        const sequence = b.sequence([]);
   409	
   410	        for (const binding of metadata.references) {
   411	                if (binding.kind === 'normal' && binding.declaration_kind !== 'import') {
   412	                        continue;
   413	                }
   414	
   415	                var getter = build_getter({ ...binding.node }, state);
   416	
   417	                if (
   418	                        binding.kind === 'bindable_prop' ||
   419	                        binding.kind === 'template' ||
   420	                        binding.declaration_kind === 'import' ||
   421	                        binding.node.name === '$$props' ||
   422	                        binding.node.name === '$$restProps'
   423	                ) {
   424	                        getter = b.call('$.deep_read_state', getter);
   425	                }
   426	
   427	                sequence.expressions.push(getter);
   428	        }
   429	
   430	        sequence.expressions.push(b.call('$.untrack', b.thunk(value)));
   431	
   432	        return sequence;
   433	}
   434	
   435	/**
   436	 * Wraps a statement/expression with dev stack tracking in dev mode
   437	 * @param {Expression} expression - The function call to wrap (e.g., $.if, $.each, etc.)
   438	 * @param {{ start?: number }} node - AST node for location info
   439	 * @param {'component' | 'if' | 'each' | 'await' | 'key' | 'render'} type - Type of block/component
   440	 * @param {Record<string, number | string>} [additional] - Any additional properties to add to the dev stack entry
   441	 * @returns {ExpressionStatement} - Statement with or without dev stack wrapping
   442	 */
   443	export function add_svelte_meta(expression, node, type, additional) {
   444	        if (!dev) {
   445	                return b.stmt(expression);
   446	        }
   447	
   448	        const location = node.start !== undefined && locator(node.start);
   449	        if (!location) {
   450	                return b.stmt(expression);
   451	        }
   452	
   453	        return b.stmt(
   454	                b.call(
   455	                        '$.add_svelte_meta',
   456	                        b.arrow([], expression),
   457	                        b.literal(type),
   458	                        b.id(component_name),
   459	                        b.literal(location.line),
   460	                        b.literal(location.column),
   461	                        additional && b.object(Object.entries(additional).map(([k, v]) => b.init(k, b.literal(v))))
   462	                )
   463	        );
   464	}

     1	/** @import { AssignmentPattern, BlockStatement, Expression, Identifier, Statement } from 'estree' */
     2	/** @import { AST } from '#compiler' */
     3	/** @import { ComponentContext } from '../types' */
     4	import { dev } from '../../../../state.js';
     5	import { extract_paths } from '../../../../utils/ast.js';
     6	import * as b from '#compiler/builders';
     7	import { get_value } from './shared/declarations.js';
     8	
     9	/**
    10	 * @param {AST.SnippetBlock} node
    11	 * @param {ComponentContext} context
    12	 */
    13	export function SnippetBlock(node, context) {
    14	        // TODO hoist where possible
    15	        /** @type {(Identifier | AssignmentPattern)[]} */
    16	        const args = [b.id('$$anchor')];
    17	        const has_await = node.body.metadata.has_await || false;
    18	
    19	        /** @type {BlockStatement} */
    20	        let body;
    21	
    22	        /** @type {Statement[]} */
    23	        const declarations = [];
    24	
    25	        const transform = { ...context.state.transform };
    26	        const child_state = { ...context.state, transform };
    27	
    28	        for (let i = 0; i < node.parameters.length; i++) {
    29	                const argument = node.parameters[i];
    30	
    31	                if (!argument) continue;
    32	
    33	                if (argument.type === 'Identifier') {
    34	                        args.push(b.assignment_pattern(argument, b.id('$.noop')));
    35	                        transform[argument.name] = { read: b.call };
    36	
    37	                        continue;
    38	                }
    39	
    40	                let arg_alias = `$$arg${i}`;
    41	                args.push(b.id(arg_alias));
    42	
    43	                const { inserts, paths } = extract_paths(argument, b.maybe_call(b.id(arg_alias)));
    44	
    45	                for (const { id, value } of inserts) {
    46	                        id.name = context.state.scope.generate('$$array');
    47	                        transform[id.name] = { read: get_value };
    48	
    49	                        declarations.push(
    50	                                b.var(id, b.call('$.derived', /** @type {Expression} */ (context.visit(b.thunk(value)))))
    51	                        );
    52	                }
    53	
    54	                for (const path of paths) {
    55	                        const name = /** @type {Identifier} */ (path.node).name;
    56	                        const needs_derived = path.has_default_value; // to ensure that default value is only called once
    57	                        const fn = b.thunk(/** @type {Expression} */ (context.visit(path.expression, child_state)));
    58	
    59	                        declarations.push(b.let(path.node, needs_derived ? b.call('$.derived_safe_equal', fn) : fn));
    60	
    61	                        transform[name] = {
    62	                                read: needs_derived ? get_value : b.call
    63	                        };
    64	
    65	                        // we need to eagerly evaluate the expression in order to hit any
    66	                        // 'Cannot access x before initialization' errors
    67	                        if (dev) {
    68	                                declarations.push(b.stmt(transform[name].read(b.id(name))));
    69	                        }
    70	                }
    71	        }
    72	        const block = /** @type {BlockStatement} */ (context.visit(node.body, child_state)).body;
    73	        body = b.block([
    74	                dev ? b.stmt(b.call('$.validate_snippet_args', b.spread(b.id('arguments')))) : b.empty,
    75	                ...declarations,
    76	                ...block
    77	        ]);
    78	
    79	        // in dev we use a FunctionExpression (not arrow function) so we can use `arguments`
    80	        let snippet = dev
    81	                ? b.call(
    82	                                '$.wrap_snippet',
    83	                                b.id(context.state.analysis.name),
    84	                                b.function(null, args, body, has_await)
    85	                        )
    86	                : b.arrow(args, body, has_await);
    87	
    88	        const declaration = b.const(node.expression, snippet);
    89	
    90	        // Top-level snippets are hoisted so they can be referenced in the `<script>`
    91	        if (context.path.length === 1 && context.path[0].type === 'Fragment') {
    92	                if (node.metadata.can_hoist) {
    93	                        context.state.module_level_snippets.push(declaration);
    94	                } else {
    95	                        context.state.instance_level_snippets.push(declaration);
    96	                }
    97	        } else {
    98	                context.state.init.push(declaration);
    99	        }
   100	}

=== Compiled JavaScript ===
import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import 'svelte/internal/flags/async';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root_1 = $.from_html(`<p> </p>`);
var root_2 = $.from_html(`<p>pending</p>`);

export default function Test_snippet_async($$anchor) {
	async function getValue() {
		return 'test value';
	}

	const value = getValue();
	var fragment = $.comment();
	var node = $.first_child(fragment);

	{
		const content = ($$anchor) => {
			var p = root_1();
			var text = $.child(p, true);

			$.reset(p);
			$.template_effect(($0) => $.set_text(text, $0), undefined, [() => value]);
			$.append($$anchor, p);
		};

		const pending = ($$anchor) => {
			var p_1 = root_2();

			$.append($$anchor, p_1);
		};

		$.boundary(node, { pending }, ($$anchor) => {
			content($$anchor);
		});
	}

	$.append($$anchor, fragment);
}

Excellent! Now I can see the issue. Look at this line:

```javascript
$.template_effect(($0) => $.set_text(text, $0), undefined, [() => value]);
```

The problem is that:
1. The `await value` expression in the snippet is being tracked as an async value
2. The template_effect is called with parameters `($0)` - expecting one parameter
3. But the order is: `sync_values()`, then `async_values()`
4. Since `value` has `await`, it's in `async_values()`, which is the third parameter to template_effect
5. However, the second parameter is `undefined` (no sync values), and the third parameter is `[() => value]`

The issue is that in the snippet, the `value` is referenced without awaiting it first inside the snippet's own context. Let me look at what the expected output should be. Let me create a simpler test case:

	{/snippet}

	<!-- value is awaited when calling the snippet -->
	{@render content()}

/**
 * @param {'$effect' | '$effect.pre' | '$inspect'} rune
 */
export function validate_effect(rune) {
	if (active_effect === null && active_reaction === null) {
		e.effect_orphan(rune);
	}

	if (active_reaction !== null && (active_reaction.f & UNOWNED) !== 0 && active_effect === null) {
		e.effect_in_unowned_derived();
	}

	if (is_destroying_effect) {
		e.effect_in_teardown(rune);
	}
}

OBSERVATION:

export function flatten(sync, async, fn) {
	const d = is_runes() ? derived : derived_safe_equal;

	if (async.length === 0) {
		fn(sync.map(d));
		return;
	}

	var batch = current_batch;
	var parent = /** @type {Effect} */ (active_effect);

	var restore = capture();
	var boundary = get_pending_boundary();

	Promise.all(async.map((expression) => async_derived(expression)))
		.then((result) => {
			batch?.activate();

			restore();

			try {
				fn([...sync.map(d), ...result]);
			} catch (error) {
				// ignore errors in blocks that have already been destroyed
				if ((parent.f & DESTROYED) === 0) {
					invoke_error_boundary(error, parent);
				}
			}

			batch?.deactivate();
			unset_context();
		})
		.catch((error) => {
			boundary.error(error);
		});
}

/**
 * Captures the current effect context so that we can restore it after
 * some asynchronous work has happened (so that e.g. `await a + b`
 * causes `b` to be registered as a dependency).
 */
function capture() {
	var previous_effect = active_effect;
	var previous_reaction = active_reaction;
	var previous_component_context = component_context;

	return function restore() {
		set_active_effect(previous_effect);
		set_active_reaction(previous_reaction);
		set_component_context(previous_component_context);

Ah! Now I see the issue! Look at this line in the `flatten` function:

```javascript
fn([...sync.map(d), ...result]);
```

The function is calling `fn` with the combined array: `[...sync.map(d), ...result]` where sync values come first, then async values.

But after the fix in commit acd9eaf2e, the `memoizer.apply()` function returns `[...this.#sync, ...this.#async]`, which means the IDs are assigned in order: sync first, then async. This is correct.

However, the issue is that when compiling the snippet, the template_effect is being created inside the snippet body, but the `value` variable reference is in the async array. The problem is that the snippet function doesn't have access to the outer scope's `value` variable directly.

Let me look at how the snippet is being compiled more carefully. The issue is that the snippet creates its own scope, and the `await value` expression inside the snippet is being tracked, but the `value` itself is defined in the parent component scope, not in the snippet's scope.

Let me look at how the compiler handles variable scoping in snippets:

import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import 'svelte/internal/flags/async';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root_1 = $.from_html(`<p>pending</p>`);
var root_2 = $.from_html(`<p> </p>`);

export default function Main($$anchor) {
	function foo() {
		return 'foo';
	}

	async function bar() {
		return Promise.resolve('bar');
	}

	var fragment = $.comment();
	var node = $.first_child(fragment);

	{
		const pending = ($$anchor) => {
			var p = root_1();

			$.append($$anchor, p);
		};

		$.boundary(node, { pending }, ($$anchor) => {
			var p_1 = root_2();
			var text = $.child(p_1);

			$.reset(p_1);
			$.template_effect(($0, $1) => $.set_text(text, `${$0 ?? ''} ${$1 ?? ''}`), [foo], [bar]);
			$.append($$anchor, p_1);
		});
	}

	$.append($$anchor, fragment);
}

Now I can see the problem clearly!

In the snippet `content`, we have:
```javascript
$.template_effect(($0) => $.set_text(text, $0), undefined, [() => value]);
```

The template_effect expects:
- First param: callback with parameters `$0`
- Second param: `undefined` (no sync values)
- Third param: `[() => value]` (async values)

According to the `flatten` function in async.js:
```javascript
fn([...sync.map(d), ...result]);
```

This means the callback will be called with an array like `[...[], ...result]` which is just `[result[0]]`. So `$0` should get the value of `await value`. But the problem is that `value` is being referenced inside the snippet but it's defined in the parent scope!

Wait, let me look more carefully at the code. The `value` variable is being captured in a closure `[() => value]`. This should work fine! Let me trace through what's happening.

Looking back at the Memoizer code and the change that was made, I realize the issue now! When the order was changed from `[...this.#async, ...this.#sync]` to `[...this.#sync, ...this.#async]`, the IDs are being reassigned numbers in a different order, but the positional arguments in the callbacks are still expecting the old order!

Wait, that's not quite right either. Let me look more carefully at the memoizer apply() method:

```javascript
apply() {
    return [...this.#sync, ...this.#async].map((memo, i) => {
        memo.id.name = `$${i}`;
        return memo.id;
    });
}
```

This returns the IDs in the order: sync IDs first, then async IDs.

And `template_effect` is called as:
```javascript
$.template_effect(
    b.arrow(
        ids,  // <-- this is the result of memoizer.apply()
        // ...
    ),
    memoizer.sync_values(),
    memoizer.async_values()
)
```

So if there are no sync values and only async values, `ids` would be `[$0]` (the single async ID).

But then `flatten` is called with:
- `sync = []` (empty, from `memoizer.sync_values()` returning `undefined`)
- `async = [() => value]` (from `memoizer.async_values()`)

And `flatten` does:
```javascript
fn([...sync.map(d), ...result]);
```

Which would be `fn([...[], ...result])` = `fn([result[0]])` where `result[0]` is the async_derived of `() => value`.

This should be fine! But wait... let me check what happens when `sync_values()` returns `undefined`:

     7	import { transform_template } from '../transform-template/index.js';
     8	import { process_children } from './shared/fragment.js';
     9	import { build_render_statement, Memoizer } from './shared/utils.js';
    10	import { Template } from '../transform-template/template.js';
    11	
    12	/**
    13	 * @param {AST.Fragment} node
    14	 * @param {ComponentContext} context
    15	 */
    16	export function Fragment(node, context) {
    17	        // Creates a new block which looks roughly like this:
    18	        // ```js
    19	        // // hoisted:
    20	        // const block_name = $.from_html(`...`);
    21	        //
    22	        // // for the main block:
    23	        // const id = block_name();
    24	        // // init stuff and possibly render effect
    25	        // $.append($$anchor, id);
    26	        // ```
    27	        // Adds the hoisted parts to `context.state.hoisted` and returns the statements of the main block.
    28	
    29	        const parent = context.path.at(-1) ?? node;
    30	
    31	        const namespace = infer_namespace(context.state.metadata.namespace, parent, node.nodes);
    32	
    33	        const { hoisted, trimmed, is_standalone, is_text_first } = clean_nodes(
    34	                parent,
    35	                node.nodes,
    36	                context.path,
    37	                namespace,
    38	                context.state,
    39	                context.state.preserve_whitespace,
    40	                context.state.options.preserveComments
    41	        );
    42	
    43	        if (hoisted.length === 0 && trimmed.length === 0) {
    44	                return b.block([]);
    45	        }
    46	
    47	        const is_single_element = trimmed.length === 1 && trimmed[0].type === 'RegularElement';
    48	        const is_single_child_not_needing_template =
    49	                trimmed.length === 1 &&
    50	                (trimmed[0].type === 'SvelteFragment' || trimmed[0].type === 'TitleElement');
    51	        const has_await = context.state.init !== null && (node.metadata.has_await || false);
    52	
    53	        const template_name = context.state.scope.root.unique('root'); // TODO infer name from parent
    54	
    55	        /** @type {Statement[]} */
    56	        const body = [];
    57	
    58	        /** @type {Statement | undefined} */
    59	        let close = undefined;
    60	
    61	        /** @type {ComponentClientTransformState} */
    62	        const state = {
    63	                ...context.state,
    64	                init: [],
    65	                consts: [],
    66	                update: [],
    67	                after_update: [],
    68	                memoizer: new Memoizer(),
    69	                template: new Template(),
    70	                transform: { ...context.state.transform },
    71	                metadata: {
    72	                        namespace,
    73	                        bound_contenteditable: context.state.metadata.bound_contenteditable
    74	                }
    75	        };
    76	
    77	        for (const node of hoisted) {
    78	                context.visit(node, state);
    79	        }
    80	
    81	        if (is_single_element) {
    82	                const element = /** @type {AST.RegularElement} */ (trimmed[0]);
    83	
    84	                const id = b.id(context.state.scope.generate(element.name));
    85	
    86	                context.visit(element, {
    87	                        ...state,
    88	                        node: id
    89	                });
    90	
    91	                let flags = state.template.needs_import_node ? TEMPLATE_USE_IMPORT_NODE : undefined;
    92	
    93	                const template = transform_template(state, namespace, flags);
    94	                state.hoisted.push(b.var(template_name, template));
    95	
    96	                state.init.unshift(b.var(id, b.call(template_name)));
    97	                close = b.stmt(b.call('$.append', b.id('$$anchor'), id));
    98	        } else if (is_single_child_not_needing_template) {
    99	                context.visit(trimmed[0], state);
   100	        } else if (trimmed.length === 1 && trimmed[0].type === 'Text') {
   101	                const id = b.id(context.state.scope.generate('text'));
   102	                state.init.unshift(b.var(id, b.call('$.text', b.literal(trimmed[0].data))));
   103	                close = b.stmt(b.call('$.append', b.id('$$anchor'), id));
   104	        } else if (trimmed.length > 0) {
   105	                const id = b.id(context.state.scope.generate('fragment'));
   106	
   107	                const use_space_template =
   108	                        trimmed.some((node) => node.type === 'ExpressionTag') &&
   109	                        trimmed.every((node) => node.type === 'Text' || node.type === 'ExpressionTag');
   110	
   111	                if (use_space_template) {
   112	                        // special case — we can use `$.text` instead of creating a unique template
   113	                        const id = b.id(context.state.scope.generate('text'));
   114	
   115	                        process_children(trimmed, () => id, false, {
   116	                                ...context,
   117	                                state
   118	                        });
   119	
   120	                        state.init.unshift(b.var(id, b.call('$.text')));
   121	                        close = b.stmt(b.call('$.append', b.id('$$anchor'), id));
   122	                } else {
   123	                        if (is_standalone) {
   124	                                // no need to create a template, we can just use the existing block's anchor
   125	                                process_children(trimmed, () => b.id('$$anchor'), false, { ...context, state });
   126	                        } else {
   127	                                /** @type {(is_text: boolean) => Expression} */
   128	                                const expression = (is_text) => b.call('$.first_child', id, is_text && b.true);
   129	
   130	                                process_children(trimmed, expression, false, { ...context, state });
   131	
   132	                                let flags = TEMPLATE_FRAGMENT;
   133	
   134	                                if (state.template.needs_import_node) {
   135	                                        flags |= TEMPLATE_USE_IMPORT_NODE;
   136	                                }
   137	
   138	                                if (state.template.nodes.length === 1 && state.template.nodes[0].type === 'comment') {
   139	                                        // special case — we can use `$.comment` instead of creating a unique template
   140	                                        state.init.unshift(b.var(id, b.call('$.comment')));
   141	                                } else {
   142	                                        const template = transform_template(state, namespace, flags);
   143	                                        state.hoisted.push(b.var(template_name, template));
   144	
   145	                                        state.init.unshift(b.var(id, b.call(template_name)));
   146	                                }
   147	
   148	                                close = b.stmt(b.call('$.append', b.id('$$anchor'), id));
   149	                        }
   150	                }
   151	        }
   152	
   153	        body.push(...state.consts);
   154	
   155	        if (has_await) {
   156	                body.push(b.if(b.call('$.aborted'), b.return()));
   157	        }
   158	
   159	        if (is_text_first) {
   160	                // skip over inserted comment
   161	                body.push(b.stmt(b.call('$.next')));
   162	        }
   163	
   164	        body.push(...state.init);
   165	
   166	        if (state.update.length > 0) {
   167	                body.push(build_render_statement(state));
   168	        }
   169	
   170	        body.push(...state.after_update);
   171	
   172	        if (close !== undefined) {
   173	                // It's important that close is the last statement in the block, as any previous statements
   174	                // could contain element insertions into the template, which the close statement needs to
   175	                // know of when constructing the list of current inner elements.
   176	                body.push(close);
   177	        }
   178	
   179	        if (has_await) {
   180	                return b.block([b.stmt(b.call('$.async_body', b.arrow([], b.block(body), true)))]);
   181	        } else {
   182	                return b.block(body);
   183	        }
   184	}
   185

```javascript
const content = ($$anchor) => {
    var p = root_1();
    var text = $.child(p, true);

    $.reset(p);
    $.template_effect(($0) => $.set_text(text, $0), undefined, [() => value]);

```

But the error message says "Uncaught (in promise) ReferenceError: value is not defined". This means that when the code is actually executed, `value` is not in scope!

Let me think about the problem differently. The issue might be about the order of when things are defined and when they're used. Let me look at the full generated code more carefully:

```javascript
export default function Test_snippet_async($$anchor) {
    async function getValue() {
        return 'test value';
    }

    const value = getValue();
    var fragment = $.comment();
    var node = $.first_child(fragment);

    {
        const content = ($$anchor) => {
            var p = root_1();
            var text = $.child(p, true);

            $.reset(p);
            $.template_effect(($0) => $.set_text(text, $0), undefined, [() => value]);
            $.append($$anchor, p);
        };

        const pending = ($$anchor) => {
            var p_1 = root_2();

            $.append($$anchor, p_1);
        };

        $.boundary(node, { pending }, ($$anchor) => {
            content($$anchor);
        });
    }

    $.append($$anchor, fragment);
}
```

This looks fine to me. `value` is defined before `content` is defined, so the closure should have access to it.

2025-12-26 13:33:52,452 - INFO - swea-agent - 💭 THOUGHT
Now let me understand what order the template_effect is expecting. Looking at build_render_statement in utils.js:

```javascript
return b.stmt(
    b.call(
        '$.template_effect',
        b.arrow(
            ids,  // this is from memoizer.apply()
            ...
        ),
        memoizer.sync_values(),
        memoizer.async_values()
    )
);
```

So the template_effect is called with:
1. A function with parameters `ids` (from memoizer.apply())
2. `memoizer.sync_values()` - the sync expressions
3. `memoizer.async_values()` - the async expressions

And in flatten:
```javascript
fn([...sync.map(d), ...result]);
```

This means the function `fn` is called with sync values first, then async values. So the IDs should also be in sync-then-async order.

Before the fix:
- `memoizer.apply()` returned `[...async, ...sync]` (async IDs first)
- But template_effect was called with `(fn, sync, async)`
- And flatten would call `fn([...sync, ...async])` (sync values first)
- So there was a mismatch!

After the fix:
- `memoizer.apply()` returns `[...sync, ...async]` (sync IDs first)
- template_effect is called with `(fn, sync, async)`
- flatten calls `fn([...sync, ...async])` (sync values first)
- So now they match!

This makes sense. But then why would the snippet code break? Let me look at my test case again more carefully. Actually, let me see what gets compiled when there's a mix of sync and async values inside a snippet:

</script>

<svelte:boundary>
	{#snippet content()}
		<p>{syncValue} {await value}</p>
	{/snippet}

	{@render content()}

	{#snippet pending()}
		<p>pending</p>
	{/snippet}
</svelte:boundary>

=== Compiled JavaScript ===
import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import 'svelte/internal/flags/async';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root_1 = $.from_html(`<p> </p>`);
var root_2 = $.from_html(`<p>pending</p>`);

export default function Test_snippet_async_mixed($$anchor) {
	async function getValue() {
		return 'async value';
	}

	const value = getValue();
	const syncValue = 'sync value';
	var fragment = $.comment();
	var node = $.first_child(fragment);

	{
		const content = ($$anchor) => {
			var p = root_1();
			var text = $.child(p);

			$.reset(p);
			$.template_effect(($0) => $.set_text(text, `sync value ${$0 ?? ''}`), undefined, [() => value]);
			$.append($$anchor, p);
		};

		const pending = ($$anchor) => {
			var p_1 = root_2();

			$.append($$anchor, p_1);
		};

		$.boundary(node, { pending }, ($$anchor) => {
			content($$anchor);
		});
	}

	$.append($$anchor, fragment);
}

=== Compiled JavaScript ===
import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import 'svelte/internal/flags/async';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root_1 = $.from_html(`<p> </p>`);
var root_2 = $.from_html(`<p>pending</p>`);

export default function Test_snippet_async_mixed2($$anchor) {
	async function getValue() {
		return 'async value';
	}

	function getSyncValue() {
		return 'sync value';
	}

	const value = getValue();
	const syncValue = getSyncValue();
	var fragment = $.comment();
	var node = $.first_child(fragment);

	{
		const content = ($$anchor) => {
			var p = root_1();
			var text = $.child(p);

			$.reset(p);
			$.template_effect(($0) => $.set_text(text, `${syncValue ?? ''} ${$0 ?? ''}`), undefined, [() => value]);
			$.append($$anchor, p);
		};

		const pending = ($$anchor) => {
			var p_1 = root_2();

			$.append($$anchor, p_1);
		};

		$.boundary(node, { pending }, ($$anchor) => {
			content($$anchor);
		});
	}

	$.append($$anchor, fragment);
}

import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import 'svelte/internal/flags/async';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root_1 = $.from_html(`<p> </p>`);
var root_2 = $.from_html(`<p>pending</p>`);

export default function Test_snippet_async_mixed3($$anchor) {
	async function getAsyncValue() {
		return 'async value';
	}

	function getSyncValue() {
		return 'sync value';
	}

	var fragment = $.comment();
	var node = $.first_child(fragment);

	{
		const content = ($$anchor) => {
			var p = root_1();
			var text = $.child(p);

			$.reset(p);
			$.template_effect(($0, $1) => $.set_text(text, `${$0 ?? ''} ${$1 ?? ''}`), [getSyncValue], [getAsyncValue]);
			$.append($$anchor, p);
		};

		const pending = ($$anchor) => {
			var p_1 = root_2();

			$.append($$anchor, p_1);
		};

		$.boundary(node, { pending }, ($$anchor) => {
			content($$anchor);
		});
	}

	$.append($$anchor, fragment);
}

$.template_effect(($0, $1) => $.set_text(text, `${$1 ?? ''} ${$0 ?? ''}`), [getSyncValue], [getAsyncValue]);

- `$0` mapped to async value (getAsyncValue) 
- `$1` mapped to sync value (getSyncValue)

But the template is expecting them in source order (getSyncValue first, then getAsyncValue), so it used `$1` (sync) then `$0` (async).

After the fix in v5.38.3, the IDs are in sync-then-async order, so `$0` is sync and `$1` is async, which matches the source order, so the template uses `$0` then `$1`.

import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import 'svelte/internal/flags/async';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root_1 = $.from_html(`<p> </p>`);
var root_2 = $.from_html(`<p>pending</p>`);

export default function Test_snippet_async($$anchor) {
	async function getValue() {
		return 'test value';
	}

	const value = getValue();
	var fragment = $.comment();
	var node = $.first_child(fragment);

	{
		const content = ($$anchor) => {
			var p = root_1();
			var text = $.child(p, true);

			$.reset(p);
			$.template_effect(($0) => $.set_text(text, $0), undefined, [() => value]);
			$.append($$anchor, p);
		};

		const pending = ($$anchor) => {
			var p_1 = root_2();

			$.append($$anchor, p_1);
		};

		$.boundary(node, { pending }, ($$anchor) => {
			content($$anchor);
		});
	}

	$.append($$anchor, fragment);
}

=== Compiled JavaScript ===
import 'svelte/internal/disclose-version';
import 'svelte/internal/flags/async';
import * as $ from 'svelte/internal/client';

var root_1 = $.from_html(`<p> </p>`);
var root_2 = $.from_html(`<p>pending</p>`);

export default function Test_snippet_async_toplevel($$anchor) {
	$.async_body(async () => {
		const value = (await $.save(Promise.resolve('test value')))();

		if ($.aborted()) return;

		var fragment = $.comment();
		var node = $.first_child(fragment);

		{
			const content = ($$anchor) => {
				var p = root_1();
				var text = $.child(p, true);

				$.reset(p);
				$.template_effect(() => $.set_text(text, value));
				$.append($$anchor, p);
			};

			const pending = ($$anchor) => {
				var p_1 = root_2();

				$.append($$anchor, p_1);
			};

			$.boundary(node, { pending }, ($$anchor) => {
				content($$anchor);
			});
		}

		$.append($$anchor, fragment);
	});
}

v5.38.2:
```javascript
$.template_effect(($0, $1) => $.set_text(text, `${$1 ?? ''} ${$0 ?? ''}`), [getSyncValue], [getAsyncValue]);
```

v5.38.3:
```javascript
$.template_effect(($0, $1) => $.set_text(text, `${$0 ?? ''} ${$1 ?? ''}`), [getSyncValue], [getAsyncValue]);
```

The change in acd9eaf2e changed the order of how the IDs are assigned, BUT the template code was already expecting the IDs in sync-then-async order! So in v5.38.2, the template code was wrong (using wrong IDs), but it worked because the IDs were also in the wrong order. After the fix in v5.38.3, the IDs are in the correct order, so the template code is now correct!
